Structural properties and internal dynamics of the elliptical galaxies in Dabringhausen & Fellhauer (2015).
This is the full version of Table (14) in Dabringhausen & Fellhauer (2015). Unknown values are indictated with negative entries.

The table contains the following data:
Column 1:  The running number of the galaxy that identifies it within this catalogue.
Column 2:  The physical effective half-light radii, R_e, of the galaxies.
Column 3:  The uncertainty of R_e$.
Column 4:  The sources for R_e and its uncertainty.
Column 5:  The best-fitting Sersic-index of the galaxy.
Column 6:  The uncertainty of the Sersic index.
Column 7:  The source of the listed values for the Sersic index and its uncertainty.
Column 8:  sigma_e, the internal velocity dispersion within R_e of the galaxies.
Column 9:  The positive uncertainties of sigma_e.
Column 10: The absolute values of the negative uncertainties of sigma_e.
Column 11: The sources for sigma_e and its uncertainties.
Column 12: sigma_0, the internal velocity dispersion at the centre of the galaxies.
Column 13: The positive uncertainties of sigma_0.
Column 14: The absolute values of the negative uncertainties of sigma_0.
Column 15: The sources for sigma_0 and its uncertainties. 
Column 16: v_rot, the rotational velocities of the galaxies.
Column 17: The positive uncertainties of v_rot.
Column 18: The absolute values of the negative uncertainties of v_rot.
Column 19: The sources for v_rot and its uncertainties.
Column 20: The estimates for the dynamical mass of the ETGs, M_dyn. The number actually shown in column~20 is the logarithm to the base of 10 of M_dyn in Solar units.
Column 21: The logarithmic uncertainty to the values on M_dyn.
Column 22: The sources for the estimates on M_dyn and their uncertainties.

For a detailed description of the data in this table, see Section (7) in Dabringhausen & Fellhauer (2015).
